  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_770af285-c9de-4b50-98d3-5728a42fabec'

      $('rating_details').observe('prototip:shown', function() {
        if (this.up('#box')) {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });

<span id="freeTextContainer3712749169104205768"><i>This is a previously-published edition - ISBN13: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/48845486-the-hating-game' rel='nofollow noopener'>9780062439604</a></i><br/><br/><i>Nemesis (n.) 1) An opponent or rival whom a person cannot best or overcome.<br/>2) A person’s undoing<br/>3) Joshua Templeman</i><br/><br/>Lucy Hutton has always been certain that the nice girl can get the corner office.   <span id="freeText3712749169104205768" style="display:none"><i>This is a previously-published edition - ISBN13: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/48845486-the-hating-game" rel="nofollow noopener">9780062439604</a></i><br /><br /><i>Nemesis (n.) 1) An opponent or rival whom a person cannot best or overcome.<br />2) A person’s undoing<br />3) Joshua Templeman</i><br /><br />Lucy Hutton has always been certain that the nice girl can get the corner office. She’s charming and accommodating and prides herself on being loved by everyone at Bexley &amp; Gamin. Everyone except for coldly efficient, impeccably attired, physically intimidating Joshua Templeman. And the feeling is mutual.<br /><br />Trapped in a shared office together 40 (OK, 50 or 60) hours a week, they’ve become entrenched in an addictive, ridiculous never-ending game of one-upmanship. There’s the Staring Game. The Mirror Game. The HR Game. Lucy can’t let Joshua beat her at anything—especially when a huge new promotion goes up for the taking.<br /><br />If Lucy wins this game, she’ll be Joshua’s boss. If she loses, she’ll resign. So why is she suddenly having steamy dreams about Joshua, and dressing for work like she’s got a hot date? After a perfectly innocent elevator ride ends with an earth-shattering kiss, Lucy starts to wonder whether she’s got Joshua Templeman all wrong.<br /><br />Maybe Lucy Hutton doesn’t hate Joshua Templeman. And maybe, he doesn’t hate her either. Or maybe this is just another game.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3712749169104205768" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2081423598" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2081423598" />
    <a title="Skyler Autumn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12859342-skyler-autumn"><img alt="Skyler Autumn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1534857879p2/12859342.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2081423598?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Skyler Autumn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Skyler Autumn" href="/user/show/12859342-skyler-autumn">Skyler Autumn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/27213238-the-hating-game">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12859342-skyler-autumn?shelf=not-worth-the-hype">not-worth-the-hype</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12859342-skyler-autumn?shelf=loath">loath</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2081423598" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9066998009304909076"><b> 1 Stars </b><br/><br/><b> Warning I'm about to swear a whole fucking lot!</b><br/><br/>I am so pissed at this book and at all the people who got this book a average 4.24 rating on Goodreads. How!?! Is the author bribing people? Has she held your loved ones hostage!? <br/><br/>The novel follows the relationship of Lucy and Josh rivals in life and the "workplace." I put workplace in brackets because the two leads rarely do anything but stare at each other and play immature games in the same vain as 2 year old boy pulling the hair of a g</span>
  <span id="freeText9066998009304909076" style="display:none"><b> 1 Stars </b><br /><br /><b> Warning I'm about to swear a whole fucking lot!</b><br /><br />I am so pissed at this book and at all the people who got this book a average 4.24 rating on Goodreads. How!?! Is the author bribing people? Has she held your loved ones hostage!? <br /><br />The novel follows the relationship of Lucy and Josh rivals in life and the "workplace." I put workplace in brackets because the two leads rarely do anything but stare at each other and play immature games in the same vain as 2 year old boy pulling the hair of a girl he has a crush on. YET, they some how are up for a major promotion. Can I work here? Seems like there is a lot of drinking on the job. One day during a team building paintball day Lucy feels ill and Josh show his "sensitivity" by taking care of her. I put sensitivity in brackets because I'm tired of women giving men a fucking award for showing basic human decency. <br /><br />Other then the annoying cliche story there is a odd amount of nice guy bashing in this book. What a weird bloody stance to take Sally Thorne. Lucy is used as the barometer of why nice is a bad thing to be since her people pleasing tendencies cause people to walk all over her. I'm sorry Sally Thorne you are mistaking insecure weakness for kindness. At one point Josh tries to gain the readers sympathy by mentioning how upset he gets when people comment on how handsome he is because he's always used for his looks and then left because he has a bad personality? You mean you won the genetic lottery and the one thing you are capable of changing is what turns people away. NOBODY FEELS SORRY FOR YOU, YOU LUNATIC! <br /><br />Being an asshole needs to stop being the male leads characteristics in romances. Do you know what? Kindness is hella hot. Nice is the new sexy. Give me Peeta and Ron Weasley over moody vampires and sadistic lovers any day!!<br /><br />And WHY is everyone so fucking stunning all the time. He is basically inhumanly gorgeous and she's looks like a disney princess. Then disney princess gets all, no one will ever love me all my friends are books. It's like fuck off. You'll be fine. Also, if you didn't know this yet from reading this horrendous book. Apparently Lucy is so tiny. I don't know if the author has a concussion but I as reader don't so please stop mentioning her fucking height to me every two paragraphs. I'm not a moron. <br /><br />Also, so much sex and making out in this book!!! Such filler for the lack of story. It reads like an instruction manual. My hand pulls his hair, he thrusts... so on. It's like ya ya I know how sex works. Skip ahead. <br /><br />The good news is this book pulls itself together in the end and makes your girl heart swoon.... I'm fuck kidding the ending wraps this shit up so quickly you almost think you missed a chapter. In the end love is declared, jobs are saved and you find out that the handsome guy is actually a stalker hoarding your garbage and painting his room the colour of your eyes. I thought then the novel was going to take a cool twist and become like You by Caroline Kepnes and Josh was going to murder Lucy but no she lived and he lived and the world is now a darker place for that. <br /><br />This book likes to play with the notion that there is a thin line between love and hate and the two can easily be misconstrued. I'll have to disagree with you there because there's no confusion here I absolutely hate this fucking book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9066998009304909076" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2241235630460799107">Re-read 3/17/20: This book never fails to ease my anxieties and I love it with all of my heart. Forever indebted to this book for making me smile through the roughest times. Also, Lucy and Josh can both, like, get it<br/><br/>Re-read 5/25/19: Realized I hadn't re-read this in 2019 and obvs had to remedy that. I love this book so damn much that I could probably recite it in my sleep.   <span id="freeText2241235630460799107" style="display:none">Re-read 3/17/20: This book never fails to ease my anxieties and I love it with all of my heart. Forever indebted to this book for making me smile through the roughest times. Also, Lucy and Josh can both, like, get it<br /><br />Re-read 5/25/19: Realized I hadn't re-read this in 2019 and obvs had to remedy that. I love this book so damn much that I could probably recite it in my sleep. Swooney swoon swoon.<br /><br />Re-read 12/30/18: I had a mighty need to re-read this so it would be my last read of the year and I clearly have no regrets. I've read this book so many times now I could probably recite all the swooniest bits from memory lmao. I still love Lucy &amp; Josh 4ev@<br /><br />Re-read 9/27/18: Welp arcs of 99 Percent Mine dropped on Edelweiss so I HAD to re-read this and hi hello I still love these two jerks so damn much wow. I’m a puddle. <br /><br />Re-read 3/27/18: Do you ever just love a book so much you read it SIX TIMES? Bc same. I love Lucy 4 ev@.<br /><br />Re-read 12/30/17: Had to re-read this one last time in 2017 because I love it so damn much. Every time I re-read it I expect to like it less, but I just like it more and more and more every time. This book is my life, y’all. <br /><br />Re-read 10/31/17: Was feeling a little gloomy so I decided to re-read this book for the 4th time this year and, again, it did NOT disappoint. This book is my everything. I can’t. <br /><br />Re-read 7/16/17: Yep, I did just read this for the third time this year. That's how much I fucking love this story. Lucinda and Josh are just the cutest and this book slays me every time. Sa-woon. <br /><br />Re-read 1/28/17: Yes, my re-read of this book happened only a few weeks after completing my original read because I JUST COULDN'T HELP MYSELF. This book is adorable and phenomenal. I will say however, this re-read was done mostly via audiobook and I will say I didn't enjoy it as much that way as I did by just reading the physical book. I feel like some of the tones and inflections that narrator uses don't quite match up with the Josh/Lucinda in my head. But other than that FLAWLESS AND ADORABLE. I adore this little book.<br /><br />Original read 1/10/17: Fucking CUTE. OH MY GOD. Editing to add that while I do read a lot of romance, I rarely take any chick lit/romance seriously. THIS ONE, however, got right under my skin. I adored it. I love it in a similar way to how I love Attachments. So stinking cute.</span>

<div id="review_1749250838" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1749250838" />
    <a title="✦❋Arianna✦❋" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23370948-arianna"><img alt="✦❋Arianna✦❋" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420671997p2/23370948.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1749250838?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✦❋Arianna✦❋" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✦❋Arianna✦❋" href="/user/show/23370948-arianna">✦❋Arianna✦❋</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23370948-arianna?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23370948-arianna?shelf=top-10-of-2016">top-10-of-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23370948-arianna?shelf=romantic-comedy">romantic-comedy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1749250838" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14472164320283827689"><b>5 Stars!!</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473345361i/20451104.jpg' width='400' height='350' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>I honestly think <i>'The Hating Game”'</i> is that kind of book anyone would enjoy – wonderfully written is a very entertaining way, griping from the very beginning and perfect if you love enemies to lovers stories. I’ve read many books with this trope, so trust me when I say Sally Thorne’s debut novel was a great one. More than great actually. It was fabulous! It was fan, entertaining and so refreshing. Needless to say, I devoured this little gem from start to finish. <br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I'm twenty-eig</i></b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText14472164320283827689" style="display:none"><b>5 Stars!!</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473345361i/20451104.jpg" width="400" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I honestly think <i>'The Hating Game”'</i> is that kind of book anyone would enjoy – wonderfully written is a very entertaining way, griping from the very beginning and perfect if you love enemies to lovers stories. I’ve read many books with this trope, so trust me when I say Sally Thorne’s debut novel was a great one. More than great actually. It was fabulous! It was fan, entertaining and so refreshing. Needless to say, I devoured this little gem from start to finish. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I'm twenty-eight years old and it seems I've fallen through the cracks of heaven and hell and into purgatory. A kindergarten classroom."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>Lucy Hutton met Josh Templeman when Gamin Publishing and Bexley Books merged to avoid financial ruin. They are the executive assistants to the two owners of “Bexley &amp; Gamin” publishing house and they have been hating each other from the moment they met. Well...almost! Lucy and Josh are opposites in every way. While Lucy is sweet, fun and quirky, Josh is grumpy and cynical. From the very beginning, Lucy and Josh have been playing different games – games like ‘The Staring Game’, 'The Mirror Game’, ‘The HR Game’ and of course ‘The Hating Game’ - trying to frustrate and intimidate each other. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I should mention that the ultimate aim of all our games is to make the other smile, or cry. It’s something like that. I’ll know when I win.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>Everything seems to get worse between Lucy and Josh when they find out one of them will be the other boss. But the dynamic between them changes again with an earth shattering kiss. <br><br>This was such an awesome read! I’m not exaggerating when I’m saying this was one of the most entertaining enemies to lovers story I’ve read so far. Lucy and Josh’s story was fun, sweet and so well done. Told entirely from Lucy’s POV, <i>“The Hating Game”</i> has one of the best slow burn relationship I’ve read in a while. I loved how the relationship between these two unfolded. The transition from enemies to lovers was perfection IMO, gradual, believable and gave me tons of butterflies. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Watching you pretend to hate that nickname is the best part of my day.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>Lucy was an awesome narrator and a fantastic, endearing heroine. I loved her portrayal. She was sweet, kind, considerate and so much fun. She was a genuinely good person, a refreshing, relatable character I’m sure many readers will love from the very beginning. I think what I loved the most about her was the way she pushed Josh’s buttons. *grin* Pure entertainment! As for our male main character…Josh was so much more than I’ve initially thought he will be. He was arrogant and a little cruel, but not too much to be annoying and like Lucy he loved their “silly” games. Btw, I totally loved their games myself. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“…if I were your boss, I’d work you so fucking hard. So fucking hard.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>They were fun and enchanting and I couldn’t read fast enough to find out who will win a certain game or how their relationship will unfold. I loved Josh’s humor, his shirts...lol, his sweetness, his vulnerability and of course the fact he was a cuddler. The man was very swoon-worthy most of the time. <br><br>The witty banter between these two was fantastically done. They made me smile and grin so many times as the story progressed and I really had a great time watching them hate each other less and less and slowly falling in love. The sexual tension between these two at times was…combustible and all the sexy teasing…so good! LOVED IT!!<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“All I want to do is kiss you until I fall asleep. I want to slide in between your sheets, and find out what goes on inside your head, and underneath your clothes. I want to make a fool of myself over you.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>I really enjoyed Lucy’ POV, but I have to admit I really missed Josh’s because there were many times when I wanted so badly to be in his head. Also, I wouldn’t have minded an epilogue...just saying! <br><br>All in all, <i>'The Hating Game'</i> was a great debut novel. If you are looking for a fun, sweet enemies to lovers story, with two engaging, well developed main characters and delightful dialogue, don’t hesitate and pick this one up!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14472164320283827689" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer15069483141475170087">Reread x3. This story is one of the best things I’ve ever read. <br/><br/>-/——————————<br/><br/>Reread. <br/>My heart cannot be contained right now. I'm so in love with this book to the point where I feel sick and my heart wants to burst with happiness. This story leaves me on a high that I cannot come down from. I don't want to. I'm <i>addicted!</i> The whole thing feels so unreal to me, I'm wondering whether something like that actually exists. <br/><br/>For gods sake, I'm all over the place. <br/><br/>But, if you haven't read this book, then d</span>
  <span id="freeText15069483141475170087" style="display:none">Reread x3. This story is one of the best things I’ve ever read. <br /><br />-/——————————<br /><br />Reread. <br />My heart cannot be contained right now. I'm so in love with this book to the point where I feel sick and my heart wants to burst with happiness. This story leaves me on a high that I cannot come down from. I don't want to. I'm <i>addicted!</i> The whole thing feels so unreal to me, I'm wondering whether something like that actually exists. <br /><br />For gods sake, I'm all over the place. <br /><br />But, if you haven't read this book, then do your souls, hearts and eyes a favour and relish and swim in this incredible and hilarious story. <br /><br /><br /><b>ORIGINAL REVIEW.</b><br />I'm currently at work and I cannot, for the life of me, stop thinking about this book. It's only been a day, but I thought about it constantly before I went to bed, whilst in bed. I thought about it on my way to work and now, whilst I'm at work.<br /><br />It is safe to say that this book will be going on my all-time favourites list. I feel like it's been a while since I loved a book so ferociously, where I thought each page of it was pretty much perfect.<br /><br />And it's the author's debut novel. What?!<br /><br />Going into this, I wasn't expecting much other than a cute, flimsy love story. But the story has become absolutely ingrained in me, heart and soul. I got what I wanted and much more.<br />I don't know whether there's even much point in telling you the premise of the book itself. Or reviewing it, because words fail me completely. My feelings towards it are intense, if you haven’t gathered that already. I think it's one of the best love stories that I've had the pleasure of reading. It's hilarious, heartwarming and the development of it all is spot-on. So well done! I cannot recommend it enough.<br /><br /><b>Initial review/reaction!</b><br />WOW! OMG! WHAT DID I JUST READ?! I AM NOT FUNCTIONING RIGHT NOW! MY HEART IS ON THE VERGE OF FAILING.<br />SEND HELP!<br /><br />I feel like I can die happy right now. Actually, scratch that. Once I've experienced me some Josh Templeman myself, then I can die happy, because goddamn that man! Me emotions!<br /><br />Books like these are exactly why I have stupidly high expectations in men. In relationships in general. Damn you, fictional characters!<br /><br />And books like these are exactly why I ADORE reading. Why my soul is bound to books.</span>

<div id="review_1783626125" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1783626125" />
    <a title="emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32879029-emma"><img alt="emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520568130p2/32879029.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1783626125?book_show_action=true">Oct 26, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="emma" href="/user/show/32879029-emma">emma</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=3-stars">3-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=reread">reread</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1783626125" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1185191389526561640">Is there, like, a German word for “the experience of when something is not extremely disappointing, but it is the eleven millionth small disappointment in a year of disappointments of varying sizes and thus threatens to topple your well-being entirely”?<br/><br/>Sound off in the comments below.<br/><br/>Because, in the scheme of things, this book going from a 4.5 star read rounded up to a 3 star read is not all that consequential.<br/><br/>And yet it may be the end of everything, for me, personally, on a personal level.<br/><br/>I DON</span>
  <span id="freeText1185191389526561640" style="display:none">Is there, like, a German word for “the experience of when something is not extremely disappointing, but it is the eleven millionth small disappointment in a year of disappointments of varying sizes and thus threatens to topple your well-being entirely”?<br /><br />Sound off in the comments below.<br /><br />Because, in the scheme of things, this book going from a 4.5 star read rounded up to a 3 star read is not all that consequential.<br /><br />And yet it may be the end of everything, for me, personally, on a personal level.<br /><br />I DON’T KNOW HOW MUCH MORE I CAN TAKE.<br /><br />My original review of this is from 2016, and contains many Disney GIFs and mentions of myself grinning and also open yearning.<br /><br />If you know anything about me as I exist in 2020, you can determine for yourself that the version of me who can spiritedly and unironically include golden-age Saturday Night Live GIFs in a five star review of a romance novel is long dead.<br /><br />This is still a cute-adjacent book. We follow Lucy, who is tiny and has a lot of hair, and Josh, who is very large and very handsome.<br /><br />(In 2016, I was more able to overlook the fact that these physical attributes are their defining descriptive characteristics than I am today, in this economy.)<br /><br />The vehemence with which I hate tiny spritely Tinker Bell-esque romantic leads who ~just don’t know they’re beautiful~ has only grown in the last four years, as I have continued to be a tall girl who can only uphold a manic pixie dream façade for a few dates max.<br /><br />And while I feel roughly the same degree of hatred for male characters who are accidental assholes now as then, I find the ultimate explanation less charming / believable. See above: four years of exposure to dating.<br /><br />The smut in this book is unparalleled in terms of me being able to read it without blushing and skipping to when it’s over (and I’m no prude - I just truly hate reading words including but not limited to girth / member / length / etc.). And I do have gushy heart-swell-y moments while reading it.<br /><br />But mostly I think this was a letdown. And these characters are mean to each other. And I think just are really really really into the idea of boning each other, more than they are in love.<br /><br />There is not a scrap of evidence to disprove this point in the whole book.<br /><br />Bottom line: Can someone lend me a megaphone? I want to emit a piercing shriek and I want everyone to hear it.<br /><br />Read my original cheery review <a href="https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.com/2017/02/08/the-hating-game-review/" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=crush-worthy-boys">crush-worthy-boys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=hilarious">hilarious</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=2016-favorites">2016-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=harpercollins">harpercollins</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=aussies">aussies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=august">august</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1743496583" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15882112295425032893">This is somehow a magical blend of adult <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/42559.Sarra_Manning' title='Sarra Manning' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sarra Manning</a> + <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/19909.Sarah_Mayberry' title='Sarah Mayberry' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sarah Mayberry</a> + <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/19005.Jennifer_Crusie' title='Jennifer Crusie' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jennifer Crusie</a>. It's funny and sharp and serious, with seething workplace rivalry and career drama coupled with <b>crazy great chemistry</b> and delicious banter. It also has unbelievably <b>sweet and tender </b>moments <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[one of my favorite parts is them simply holding hands <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, though you'll easily laugh a minute after that! It captures that weird obsessive behavior you can't help when you first fall in love,</span>
  <span id="freeText15882112295425032893" style="display:none">This is somehow a magical blend of adult <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/42559.Sarra_Manning" title="Sarra Manning" rel="nofollow noopener">Sarra Manning</a> + <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/19909.Sarah_Mayberry" title="Sarah Mayberry" rel="nofollow noopener">Sarah Mayberry</a> + <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/19005.Jennifer_Crusie" title="Jennifer Crusie" rel="nofollow noopener">Jennifer Crusie</a>. It's funny and sharp and serious, with seething workplace rivalry and career drama coupled with <b>crazy great chemistry</b> and delicious banter. It also has unbelievably <b>sweet and tender </b>moments <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[one of my favorite parts is them simply holding hands <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, though you'll easily laugh a minute after that! It captures that weird obsessive behavior you can't help when you first fall in love, and also convinces you that after a hard-won relationship, these two won't ever stop being endearingly, ridiculously fussy over each other. Hate-to-love relationships are so fun when they're done well, and this is the best one I've read, in no small part because the "hate" part is pretty convincing in the beginning. It hits all the tropes and scenarios you've read before, but the <i>way</i> they're done here is just irresistible. <br /><br />Katy's review also talks a lot about the heroine's feelings of loneliness and failure, as well as the way a big argument between them is resolved: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1735828967">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a> I feel so much affection for them both--it's one of those things where you come out so pleased that they found each other. <br /><br />In short, it's basically everything you could possibly want out of a romance, with the added benefit of having so many cute and quirky details in it. <b>I felt giddy with happiness </b>reading this book, and I kept trying to prolong the experience because I know it's the author's only book...so far! I can't wait until the next one. &lt;3 Hurry up, Thorne #2.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15882112295425032893" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1911948639" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1911948639" />
    <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe"><img alt="Natalie Monroe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339730817p2/6688207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1911948639?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie Monroe" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe">Natalie Monroe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=cheesy-cheesy-cheesy">cheesy-cheesy-cheesy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=hate-the-characters-hate-the-book">hate-the-characters-hate-the-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=not-worth-the-hype">not-worth-the-hype</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=dishonor-on-your-cow">dishonor-on-your-cow</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=protagonists-i-want-to-laser-face">protagonists-i-want-to-laser-face</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=not-as-good-as-i-expected">not-as-good-as-i-expected</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=typical">typical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=wtf-concepts">wtf-concepts</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1911948639" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2324935183121555277"><b>Things that Make Natalie want to Flip a Table:<br/><br/>-Cliches</b><br/><br/><u>Cliche A: the hate-to-love relationship</u> <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1488370006ra/22105704.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This is a trope that CAN be done well. If there's a fresh spin. And the characters were likable. Josh was *gasp* secretly in love with her all along, but instead of doing something radical like being nice, he embarks on a third-grader's idea of wooing women. He figuratively flicks boogers in her hair and breaks her crayons. <br/><br/><u>Cliche B: the sick scene from every shoujo manga</u> <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1488370006i/22105705._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Our plucky heroine is dangerous</span>
  <span id="freeText2324935183121555277" style="display:none"><b>Things that Make Natalie want to Flip a Table:<br><br>-Cliches</b><br><br><u>Cliche A: the hate-to-love relationship</u> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1488370006ra/22105704.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This is a trope that CAN be done well. If there's a fresh spin. And the characters were likable. Josh was *gasp* secretly in love with her all along, but instead of doing something radical like being nice, he embarks on a third-grader's idea of wooing women. He figuratively flicks boogers in her hair and breaks her crayons. <br><br><u>Cliche B: the sick scene from every shoujo manga</u> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1488370006i/22105705._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Our plucky heroine is dangerously ill yet still determinedly stumbling through her day because she's a trooper that way. Then a wave of dizziness hits. She slumps back against a firm chest and strong arms. It's our handsome love interest who has been nothing been awful to her since 45 pages ago. He feels her forehead while she feebly bats him away, muttering she's fine. <br><br>"Idiot," he gently reprimands her, concerned and frustrated at the same time. <br><br>He takes her home, letting her lean on him. Delirious, our heroine wonders how strange it is he's being so nice to her while he's so mean all the time. He smells nice, she absently notes. <br><br>They're in the house. He stays the weekend, cooking for her and feeding her medicine and changing her clothes. As a bonus, he cleans her house too. Still caught in the impossible state of feverish delirium, she starts telling him things she'd never tell him in real life. <br><br>Slowly, unbelievably, they begin to bond. <br><br>Yeah, I'm not writing anymore. You get the idea. FYI, I have never seen or heard of someone so sick (exempting very serious diseases) that they're incapable of functioning.<br><br><u>Cliche C: the scatterbrained, nice, perky heroine and the work-obsessed, uptight guy.</u> <br><br>I'm so tired of this dynamic. And Lucy is cute in a way that I finally understand why people hate Zooey Deschanel's characters. It's <i>overwhelming</i>. Suffocating. Lucy is like Jess from New Girl on steroids. She says silly things that no one would say in real life because they have mental filters.<br><br><b>-Weird agenda against nice guys and short guys.</b> <br><br>Lucy and Josh both agree Nice Guys are overrated. Um, no. We need more Nice Guys in fiction and real life because a healthy relationship is sexy. Plus, Lucy loves mentioning that Josh can lift her up and that somehow makes him so much better than her old boyfriends. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1488370006ra/22105706.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>-Reminding me over and over again Lucy is 5 foot tall.</b> I get it. My sister gets it. My cat fucking gets it. <br><br>I also know he's tall. Haha, cute contrast. Fucking shut up about it already. <br><br><b>-Telling me their bodies fit together for the 1,457,872th time</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1488370114i/22105726._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>-Lucy objectifying Josh to the point that HE gets uncomfortable</b> She keeps on doing it even after he voices this. <br><br>How would we react if this were in a guy's POV and he kept talking about how tight that ass is or how great her boobs are? A few times is great, welcome even. S/he thinks her partner is beautiful and sexy. But if you keep on mentioning it every time you're together, it raises eyebrows. <br><br><b>-the romance is the whole story</b> <br><br>I know it's a romance book. I know, alright. But I like to think readers have gotten a little more sophisticated in their choice of romances. Side plots involving the protagonist's family and/or career are typically told alongside the main romance plotline now. <br><br>But in The Hating Game, the only plot thread that is tied up is her and Josh's relationship. We don't find out if Lucy gets promoted. We don't find out if she goes home to visit her parents. It's like <b>those things don't matter</b>, which seems dangerously regressive. <br><br>Finally, a gif that sums up my entire reading experience:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1488370006ra/22105708.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="2324935183121555277" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1740640747" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1755328509270262440"><b>5 stars!!!</b> <br/><br/><a href='http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%209/863DAA56-0A9A-40F1-A85F-570D12C930B7_zpsbjay11cd.png.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1478007631i/21019849._SY540_.png' alt=' photo 863DAA56-0A9A-40F1-A85F-570D12C930B7_zpsbjay11cd.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>What did I love about The Hating Game? <b>Everything.</b> I loved everything about this book. There is nothing better than finishing a book by an author you’ve never read and having this flying high feeling. I feel freaking giddy right now. I listened to the audio and I couldn’t wipe the smile off my face. I got asked why I was in such a good mood more than once over the few days I listened to it. That, my friends, is an epic book! <br/><br/>What do you do when you’re the nice girl at the office w</span>
  <span id="freeText1755328509270262440" style="display:none"><b>5 stars!!!</b> <br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%209/863DAA56-0A9A-40F1-A85F-570D12C930B7_zpsbjay11cd.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1478007631i/21019849._SY540_.png" alt=" photo 863DAA56-0A9A-40F1-A85F-570D12C930B7_zpsbjay11cd.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>What did I love about The Hating Game? <b>Everything.</b> I loved everything about this book. There is nothing better than finishing a book by an author you’ve never read and having this flying high feeling. I feel freaking giddy right now. I listened to the audio and I couldn’t wipe the smile off my face. I got asked why I was in such a good mood more than once over the few days I listened to it. That, my friends, is an epic book! <br><br>What do you do when you’re the nice girl at the office who has an evil nemesis? I guess you just deal with it, and Lucy Hutton has had to deal with this for far too long. Joshua Templeman is the bane of her existence. They share an office together and it’s torture for her- but what would she do without Josh and their hating game? <br><i>
  <blockquote>I should mention that the ultimate aim of all our games is to make the other smile, or cry. It’s something like that. I’ll know when I win.<br><br><b>I type my password: IHATEJOSHUA4EV@. My previous passwords have all been variations on how much I hate Joshua. For ever.</b><br><br>We each keep a log on the other. I can only assume he does; he seems to remember all of my transgressions. Mine is a password-protected document hidden on my personal drive and it journals all the shit that has ever gone down between Joshua Templeman and me. We have each complained to HR four times over this past year. He’s received a verbal and written warning about the nickname he has for me. I’ve received two warnings; one for verbal abuse and for a juvenile prank that got out of hand. I’m not proud. </blockquote>
</i><br>You see what I mean? There is not much I love more than an epic hate-love romance/office romance. And this one is on the top of the favorites list. It’s FUN and ENTERTAINING and HILARIOUS! Joshua and Lucy are quite the pair. When they find out that they are both gunning for the same job promotion, things get even worse between them. The tension between them is at an all time high. The emotions are running like crazy and it leaves Lucy more confused than ever. <br><br>Lucy was pretty dang perfect. She narrated the story (I listened to the audio) and it was fantastic. She is wonderful. Such an entertaining heroine. And don’t even get me started on Joshua. I hated him at the start, but that didn’t come close to comparing with how much I loved him by the end! <br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Stop calling me Shortcake.”<br><br>“Watching you pretend to hate that nickname is the best part of my day.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b> <br>I was shocked that this was a debut novel. It didn’t read like a debut at all. I will be jumping to read anything else this author writes. I’m sorry that this review is a little excitable and all over the place with lots of quotes and such, but I’m so excited about this book and just gushing all over the place! If you’re a fan of love/hate troupes, love a good asshole hero and strong/fun heroine, READ THIS BOOK! Highly recommended! <br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%209/3BA4B8FB-3C28-44D8-AC8E-34CAF0DCB7B9_zpsggxtfdly.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1478007631i/21019850._SY540_.png" alt=" photo 3BA4B8FB-3C28-44D8-AC8E-34CAF0DCB7B9_zpsggxtfdly.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1755328509270262440" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3268226026" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3268226026" />
    <a title=" Teodora " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69603149-teodora"><img alt=" Teodora " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582144281p2/69603149.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3268226026?book_show_action=true">Jun 15, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Teodora " class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Teodora " href="/user/show/69603149-teodora"> Teodora </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/40382630-the-hating-game">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=on-app">on-app</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3268226026" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1190614818927779796">4.75/5 ⭐<br/><br/><b>Full review on my Blog:</b> <a href='https://thedacianshewolf.home.blog/2020/06/23/the-hating-game-by-sally-thorne/' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Dacian She-Wolf</a> 🐺<br/><blockquote>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1605628384i/30390358.jpg' width='280' height='360' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</blockquote><br/>I’ve been debating so hard on rating this book because I am really not into chick-lit novels (like, almost at all) and I feel conflicted every time I have to rate one, even though I read the bloody book on my own free will.<br/><br/>But, Jesus, I’m busted now, so what’s the point in hiding behind a finger?<br/>I enjoyed this so fucking much that I just can’t deny it.<br/><br/>I don’t know what’s gotten into me one day, I woke up normally, had an online course that</span>
  <span id="freeText1190614818927779796" style="display:none">4.75/5 ⭐<br><br><b>Full review on my Blog:</b> <a href="https://thedacianshewolf.home.blog/2020/06/23/the-hating-game-by-sally-thorne/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dacian She-Wolf</a> 🐺<br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1605628384i/30390358.jpg" width="280" height="360" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br>I’ve been debating so hard on rating this book because I am really not into chick-lit novels (like, almost at all) and I feel conflicted every time I have to rate one, even though I read the bloody book on my own free will.<br><br>But, Jesus, I’m busted now, so what’s the point in hiding behind a finger?<br>I enjoyed this so fucking much that I just can’t deny it.<br><br>I don’t know what’s gotten into me one day, I woke up normally, had an online course that I almost fell asleep to, then had some breakfast and as I was drinking my coffee I was like <i>Hm, I think I might read something romance-y.</i><br><br>And guess what? The most romance-y novel I found agreeable was a book with the title <i>
  <b>The <u>Hating</u> Game.</b>
</i><br>So, yeah, you got me. I’m a hopeless romantic, what can I say…<br><br>But lemme tell you something. That cartoon-y cover with the crooked letters and funny colours hid behind it some very funny and also very sexy action that I just…enjoyed…much. As one part of my brain was asking <i>WTF is wrong with you?</i> the other part was like <i>Read, read, read, I know you’re curious to see what are they gonna do next!</i><br><br>I was torn between the two, but this is indeed a pretty accurate explanation of what was ratting in my head during this book.<br>At this point, I might start to enjoy reading funny, sexy books, who knows?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1590396174ra/29536837.gif" width="320" height="252" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>It is ridiculously easy to read, actually.</b><br><br>I mean, I finished it in two days and a half so I think that’s my new personal record. It’s been that enjoyable.<br><br>I have this thing for hate-to-love relationships that I never seem to get over. Why is this my favourite kind of falling in love? No one knows, not even the divinities above us. The idea is that yes this was about to be good. And it actually was and it actually did not disappoint me.<br><br>It was obvious from the start that Lucy was going to be the goody-two-shoes, sunshine-y girl who does everything with energy and enthusiasm and is addicted to the fact that everyone must love her and Josh was the mean fancy-ass jerk that was going to mess with her constantly and she was going to catch on fire because he was the only person who seemed to not like her.<br><br>Honestly, after all that initial cliché, everything was bomb. The line exchange was always witty, the feelings were pretty accurate in their confusion and the falling in love was as delicious as a strawberry.<br><br>Everything that happened in this book was either extremely cute or extremely sexually tense and I loved that. I think this might be the first rom-com novel I consider re-reading one day. It was <i>precious.</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1573246193ra/28423190.gif" width="320" height="240" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>What I learned from this book though is that:<br>- First impressions will not always be as we expect them to be because not everyone is the same. First impressions are one-of-a-kind experiences that have different impacts on different persons;<br>- Don’t judge a book by its cover, no one knows for sure what exactly is going on between the pages;<br>- Even though love and hate are polar opposites, there is this excruciatingly thin line between them and they can be easily mistaking for each other;<br>- Learn how to fall in love with everything.<br><br>With all this being said, <b>The Hating Game</b> made me feel very happy while reading it so that is why I am going to reward it. I am glad I gave it a shot.<br><br><a href="https://urcdn.eu/styles/c918c0d5-c6b2-4cd7-94c7-de8ddd75ae3a_original?b" rel="nofollow noopener">Book-styled</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1190614818927779796" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1764187490" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1764187490" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1764187490?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1764187490" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12844149922119093837"><b>Heartwarming (adj.):</b><br/>Causing pleasant feelings of happiness (and silly, stupid tears you can't stop).<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1441472940ra/16113383.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>By all means, it was not a sad book. On the contrary, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25883848.The_Hating_Game' title='The Hating Game by Sally Thorne' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Hating Game</a> was <b>a funny, sweet, adorable, intoxicating office romance</b> about two sworn enemies that fell in love. And I'm crying because it filled me with so much joy, and hope and love my body can barely contain!<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1440342455ra/15964052.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Both love and hate are mirror versions of the same game-and you have to win. Why? Your heart and your ego.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>Josh is </span>
  <span id="freeText12844149922119093837" style="display:none"><b>Heartwarming (adj.):</b><br>Causing pleasant feelings of happiness (and silly, stupid tears you can't stop).<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1441472940ra/16113383.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>By all means, it was not a sad book. On the contrary, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25883848.The_Hating_Game" title="The Hating Game by Sally Thorne" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hating Game</a> was <b>a funny, sweet, adorable, intoxicating office romance</b> about two sworn enemies that fell in love. And I'm crying because it filled me with so much joy, and hope and love my body can barely contain!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1440342455ra/15964052.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Both love and hate are mirror versions of the same game-and you have to win. Why? Your heart and your ego.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Josh is Lucy's nemesis. They work together while they plot each other's murder. They play juvenile games, they keep filing complaints to Human Resources, and they make each other miserable. Their competition is tough, and with a promotion on the horizon things escalate quickly. But after one mind-blowing elevator kiss, and some unexpected kindness from Josh, Lucy starts to wonder whether beneath his cold and cruel behavior exists a Nice Guy after all, with the potential to break her heart. <br><b>The line between love and hate was never so blurry.</b><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“No one can kiss me like you do.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><b>Dear <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/15651497.Sally_Thorne" title="Sally Thorne" rel="nofollow noopener">Sally Thorne</a>, I'm yours.</b><br>I can't get rid of this ridiculously wide grin on my face, I'm one step from looking like Joker. And then I remember all those moving and sweet moments and I start crying, and people wonder who murdered my cat. I don't have a cat.<br><b>Josh and Lucy's story tugged at my heartstrings in an unexpected way.</b> They were two characters <b>beautifully crafted</b>, with their flaws and insecurities. Lucy was always sociable and charming, she wanted people to like her but in the end, she was lonely. Josh was a clinical asshole that made everyone tremble, and tiny Lucy was the only one that stood up to him. Little did she know how shy and caring he was.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Shortcake.” <br>“Stop calling me Shortcake.” <br>“Watching you pretend to hate that nickname is the best part of my day.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1474477583ra/20605357.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Hilarious banters, crackling tension, tenderness and passion,</b> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25883848.The_Hating_Game" title="The Hating Game by Sally Thorne" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hating Game</a> has everything you could ask for from a romance novel. Every single touch spoke straight to my heart, and made my blood warm and my head dizzy! There were times I forgot how to breathe, and times I couldn't help but sigh. Josh is such a dreamy guy, yummilicious and sexy and so, so <b>swoonworthy</b>!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468106063ra/19667731.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>While I would have liked a few chapters from Josh's POV, I enjoyed Lucy's narrative so much! She was such a sweet and funny and adorable person, and you could understand her reservations and her fears!<br><b>I'm so in love.</b><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“What are you imagining? Your expression is filthy.”<br>“Strangling you. Bare hands.” <br>“So that’s your kink.” <br>“Only where you’re concerned.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>If this sappy review didn't convince you to read this little gem, please do check <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1749250838?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Arianna</a>'s review! ❤︎</span>
  <a data-text-id="12844149922119093837" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2194353324" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2194353324" />
    <a title="Claudia Ramírez" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13061577-claudia-ram-rez"><img alt="Claudia Ramírez" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533869692p2/13061577.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

<div id="review_2039193457" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2039193457" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1720620-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415374035p2/1720620.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2039193457?book_show_action=true">Aug 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/1720620-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2039193457" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8856869826979351203">Normally I hate chick-lit<i>y</i> romance, but this is one of those fantastic exceptions that makes me want to reconsider my usual reluctance to read this genre.<br/>In fact, I loved it so much I started to wonder:<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1501785868ra/23498921.gif' width='350' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Apparently, I'm really late to <b>The Hating Game</b> party. <br/><i>Did my friends just not tell me about this one, or did this come out while I was undergoing all that laser hair removal? Dark times, dark times...</i><br/>At any rate, I ran across this in my ongoing quest to find funny romances that make my heart go pi</span>
  <span id="freeText8856869826979351203" style="display:none">Normally I hate chick-lit<i>y</i> romance, but this is one of those fantastic exceptions that makes me want to reconsider my usual reluctance to read this genre.<br>In fact, I loved it so much I started to wonder:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1501785868ra/23498921.gif" width="350" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Apparently, I'm really late to <b>The Hating Game</b> party. <br><i>Did my friends just not tell me about this one, or did this come out while I was undergoing all that laser hair removal? Dark times, dark times...</i><br>At any rate, I ran across this in my ongoing quest to find funny romances that make my heart go pitty-pat. <br>And nothing, <i>nothing</i>, makes my heart pitty-pat as hard as a couple who start out with a mutual disgust for each other.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1501786894ra/23499047.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Well, these two <i>definitely</i> had the loathing thing down pat. <br>It. Was. Hysterical.<br>The lengths that they went to just to make sure that they managed to get under the other's skin and crawl around on a daily basis? Perfection! By the end, there was no real reason for it other than stubborn pride, but did they let that stop them?<br><b>No. No, they did not.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1459948020ra/18677117.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But the thing that made this one special (to me) was that the story<b> and</b> the characters felt <i>complete</i>. They had families, hobbies, and issues that were separate from this <i>thing</i> that was growing between them. And this may sound odd, but my favorite thing about this book was the fact that Joshua was obsessive about diet and exercise. He was ripped because <i>*gasp*</i> he worked <i>really hard</i> at it on a daily basis. So many books/movies make it seem like the guy just has magical washboard abs that ripple in the sunlight, while he chows down on a fatty steak and washes it down with a milkshake. Bahahaha! <br><b>Bullshit.</b><br>Men don't wake up looking sexy, they've gotta work at it as much as we ladies do.<br>*cough*<br>Maybe more...?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1501790494ra/23499634.gif" width="400" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Anyway, I'm not sure what to say about this that hasn't already been said. If you're looking for a fantastic romance novel that will keep you smiling throughout, this is the book for you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8856869826979351203" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1881290211" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1881290211" />
    <a title="Navessa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18104163-navessa"><img alt="Navessa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1444162983p2/18104163.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1881290211?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Navessa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Navessa" href="/user/show/18104163-navessa">Navessa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/27213238-the-hating-game">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Navessa by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/5136858-bonnie">Bonnie</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=2017-favorites">2017-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1881290211" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9990425714903755545"><b>
  <br/>
  <blockquote>
    <i>"I wish I could use my thumbs to pull his mouth into a huge deranged grin. As the police drag me out in handcuffs I'll be screeching, <i>Smile, goddamn you.</i>"</i>
  </blockquote>
</b><br/><br/>Imagine being so riled by someone that you end up thinking things like the above on a near-hourly basis. That is the kind of relationship the male and female lead in this book have with each other. They're the executive assistants to the joint heads of their company, and are forced to share cubicle space right outside their offic</span>
  <span id="freeText9990425714903755545" style="display:none"><b>
  <br>
  <blockquote>
    <i>"I wish I could use my thumbs to pull his mouth into a huge deranged grin. As the police drag me out in handcuffs I'll be screeching, <i>Smile, goddamn you.</i>"</i>
  </blockquote>
</b><br><br>Imagine being so riled by someone that you end up thinking things like the above on a near-hourly basis. That is the kind of relationship the male and female lead in this book have with each other. They're the executive assistants to the joint heads of their company, and are forced to share cubicle space right outside their offices.<br><br>Which would be fine, if they got along. <br><br>Yeah, no. These two have antagonism down to a fine art. They're so competitive that they've created little games that they play with each other. The Staring Game - where they lock eyes and have whole silent conversations filled with insults. The Mirror Game - where the male lead subtly mimics every move the female lead makes, only on a slight time delay. The HR Game - where they threaten to report each other to the poor, frazzled woman who runs the HR department for even the slightest perceived infraction. The Spying Game - where each of them rummages through the other's desk whenever the opportunity arises. <br><br>It's childish and immature and a ridiculous way to spend your work day. I thought it frigging was hysterical. <br><br>I do, however, see where some readers might take issue with Josh, the male lead, as a romantic interest. He's pretty terrible to Lucy, the female lead, at times, especially in the beginning. And yet, for me, he never crossed the line into alpha-douche territory. Because, in his defense, Lucy is equally provocative. What he dishes out, he thinks she can take, and also give back to him in turn. Which she does, with relish. Most of the time. The only issue is that at one point she cracks, hard, breaking down into tears. It's clear when this happens that this was not Josh's intention, and that he feels genuine remorse for causing her this level of frustration. <br><br>Because, you see, throughout all these little games they play with each other, you're given the sense that some twisted part of them both <i>enjoy</i> it. Lucy actively looks for ways to one-up Josh. Or to surprise a grin out of him. Josh, for his part, is obviously trying to get a different reaction from Lucy, and it's not really clear until things begin to change between them what this reaction is. <br><br>This is a romance. It's no spoiler that things DO change between them. Love and hate are a fine line, after all. Both invoke a lot of similar mental and physiological responses. So when the line blurs between these two and all that pent up aggression between them becomes filled with the promise of a non-destructive outlet, whoa. <br><br><blockquote>"I'd participate. So well you wouldn't walk straight the next day."</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1486731905ra/21944833.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>HRRRRRNNNNN<br><br>This book was so much fun to read. I devoured it in a single session, and by the time I closed it, my face hurt from smiling. The chemistry between these two is palpable from the beginning. Lucy has a completely open, self-deprecating, hilarious inner monologue. Josh, who starts out sort of broody and mysterious, only becomes more and more attractive as you peel back his tough outer layers. <br><br>And the two of them together? Gah. <br><br>I can easily see myself re-reading this over and over again. And I cannot wait for more releases from this author. I think she'll become quite a heavy-hitter in the romance genre if she keeps up this level of work. <br><br><b><a href="http://www.thealliterates.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thealliterates/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thealliterates" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/the_alliterates/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/thealliterates/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="9990425714903755545" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
